2409/*
2410 * manages a server health-check. Returns
2411 * the time the task accepts to wait, or TIME_ETERNITY for infinity.
2412 */
2413static struct task *process_chk(struct task *t, void *context, unsigned short state)
2414{
2415 struct check *check = context;
2416
2417 if (check->type == PR_O2_EXT_CHK0xA0000000)
2418 return process_chk_proc(t, context, state);
2419 return process_chk_conn(t, context, state);
2420
2421}
2422
2423static int start_check_task(struct check *check, int mininter,
2424 int nbcheck, int srvpos)
2425{
2426 struct task *t;
2427 unsigned long thread_mask = MAX_THREADS_MASK(~0UL >> (((unsigned int)sizeof(long) * 8) - ((unsigned
int)sizeof(long) * 8)));
2428
2429 if (check->type == PR_O2_EXT_CHK0xA0000000)
2430 thread_mask = 1;
2431
2432 /* task for the check */
2433 if ((t = task_new(thread_mask)) == NULL((void*)0)) {
2434 ha_alert("Starting [%s:%s] check: out of memory.\n",
2435 check->server->proxy->id, check->server->id);
2436 return 0;
2437 }
2438
2439 check->task = t;
2440 t->process = process_chk;
2441 t->context = check;
2442
2443 if (mininter < srv_getinter(check))
2444 mininter = srv_getinter(check);
2445
2446 if (global.max_spread_checks && mininter > global.max_spread_checks)
2447 mininter = global.max_spread_checks;
2448
2449 /* check this every ms */
2450 t->expire = tick_add(now_ms, MS_TO_TICKS(mininter * srvpos / nbcheck)(mininter * srvpos / nbcheck));
2451 check->start = now;
2452 task_queue(t);
2453
2454 return 1;
2455}
2456
2457/*
2458 * Start health-check.
2459 * Returns 0 if OK, ERR_FATAL on error, and prints the error in this case.
2460 */
2461static int start_checks()
2462{
2463
2464 struct proxy *px;
2465 struct server *s;
2466 struct task *t;
2467 int nbcheck=0, mininter=0, srvpos=0;
2468
2469 /* 1- count the checkers to run simultaneously.
2470 * We also determine the minimum interval among all of those which
2471 * have an interval larger than SRV_CHK_INTER_THRES. This interval
2472 * will be used to spread their start-up date. Those which have
2473 * a shorter interval will start independently and will not dictate
2474 * too short an interval for all others.
2475 */
2476 for (px = proxies_list; px; px = px->next) {
2477 for (s = px->srv; s; s = s->next) {
2478 if (s->slowstart) {
2479 if ((t = task_new(MAX_THREADS_MASK(~0UL >> (((unsigned int)sizeof(long) * 8) - ((unsigned
int)sizeof(long) * 8))))) == NULL((void*)0)) {
2480 ha_alert("Starting [%s:%s] check: out of memory.\n", px->id, s->id);
2481 return ERR_ALERT0x10 | ERR_FATAL0x02;
2482 }
2483 /* We need a warmup task that will be called when the server
2484 * state switches from down to up.
2485 */
2486 s->warmup = t;
2487 t->process = server_warmup;
2488 t->context = s;
2489 /* server can be in this state only because of */
2490 if (s->next_state == SRV_ST_STARTING)
2491 task_schedule(s->warmup, tick_add(now_ms, MS_TO_TICKS(MAX(1000, (now.tv_sec - s->last_change)) / 20)((((1000)>((now.tv_sec - s->last_change)))?(1000):((now
.tv_sec - s->last_change))) / 20)));
2492 }
2493
2494 if (s->check.state & CHK_ST_CONFIGURED0x0002) {
2495 nbcheck++;
2496 if ((srv_getinter(&s->check) >= SRV_CHK_INTER_THRES1000) &&
2497 (!mininter || mininter > srv_getinter(&s->check)))
2498 mininter = srv_getinter(&s->check);
2499 }
2500
2501 if (s->agent.state & CHK_ST_CONFIGURED0x0002) {
2502 nbcheck++;
2503 if ((srv_getinter(&s->agent) >= SRV_CHK_INTER_THRES1000) &&
2504 (!mininter || mininter > srv_getinter(&s->agent)))
2505 mininter = srv_getinter(&s->agent);
2506 }
2507 }
2508 }
2509
2510 if (!nbcheck)
2511 return 0;
2512
2513 srand((unsigned)time(NULL((void*)0)));
2514
2515 /*
2516 * 2- start them as far as possible from each others. For this, we will
2517 * start them after their interval set to the min interval divided by
2518 * the number of servers, weighted by the server's position in the list.
2519 */
2520 for (px = proxies_list; px; px = px->next) {
2521 if ((px->options2 & PR_O2_CHK_ANY0xF0000000) == PR_O2_EXT_CHK0xA0000000) {
2522 if (init_pid_list()) {
2523 ha_alert("Starting [%s] check: out of memory.\n", px->id);
2524 return ERR_ALERT0x10 | ERR_FATAL0x02;
2525 }
2526 }
2527
2528 for (s = px->srv; s; s = s->next) {
2529 /* A task for the main check */
2530 if (s->check.state & CHK_ST_CONFIGURED0x0002) {
2531 if (s->check.type == PR_O2_EXT_CHK0xA0000000) {
2532 if (!prepare_external_check(&s->check))
2533 return ERR_ALERT0x10 | ERR_FATAL0x02;
2534 }
2535 if (!start_check_task(&s->check, mininter, nbcheck, srvpos))
2536 return ERR_ALERT0x10 | ERR_FATAL0x02;
2537 srvpos++;
2538 }
2539
2540 /* A task for a auxiliary agent check */
2541 if (s->agent.state & CHK_ST_CONFIGURED0x0002) {
2542 if (!start_check_task(&s->agent, mininter, nbcheck, srvpos)) {
2543 return ERR_ALERT0x10 | ERR_FATAL0x02;
2544 }
2545 srvpos++;
2546 }
2547 }
2548 }
2549 return 0;
2550}
2551
2552/*
2553 * Perform content verification check on data in s->check.buffer buffer.
2554 * The buffer MUST be terminated by a null byte before calling this function.
2555 * Sets server status appropriately. The caller is responsible for ensuring
2556 * that the buffer contains at least 13 characters. If <done> is zero, we may
2557 * return 0 to indicate that data is required to decide of a match.
2558 */
2559static int httpchk_expect(struct server *s, int done)
2560{
2561 static THREAD_LOCAL__thread char status_msg[] = "HTTP status check returned code <000>";
2562 char status_code[] = "000";
2563 char *contentptr;
2564 int crlf;
2565 int ret;
2566
2567 switch (s->proxy->options2 & PR_O2_EXP_TYPE0x03800000) {
2568 case PR_O2_EXP_STS0x00800000:
2569 case PR_O2_EXP_RSTS0x01000000:
2570 memcpy(status_code, b_head(&s->check.bi) + 9, 3);
2571 memcpy(status_msg + strlen(status_msg) - 4, b_head(&s->check.bi) + 9, 3);
2572
2573 if ((s->proxy->options2 & PR_O2_EXP_TYPE0x03800000) == PR_O2_EXP_STS0x00800000)
2574 ret = strncmp(s->proxy->expect_str, status_code, 3) == 0;
2575 else
2576 ret = regex_exec(s->proxy->expect_regex, status_code);
2577
2578 /* we necessarily have the response, so there are no partial failures */
2579 if (s->proxy->options2 & PR_O2_EXP_INV0x04000000)
2580 ret = !ret;
2581
2582 set_server_check_status(&s->check, ret ? HCHK_STATUS_L7OKD : HCHK_STATUS_L7STS, status_msg);
2583 break;
2584
2585 case PR_O2_EXP_STR0x01800000:
2586 case PR_O2_EXP_RSTR0x02000000:
2587 /* very simple response parser: ignore CR and only count consecutive LFs,
2588 * stop with contentptr pointing to first char after the double CRLF or
2589 * to '\0' if crlf < 2.
2590 */
2591 crlf = 0;
2592 for (contentptr = b_head(&s->check.bi); *contentptr; contentptr++) {
2593 if (crlf >= 2)
2594 break;
2595 if (*contentptr == '\r')
2596 continue;
2597 else if (*contentptr == '\n')
2598 crlf++;
2599 else
2600 crlf = 0;
2601 }
2602
2603 /* Check that response contains a body... */
2604 if (crlf < 2) {
2605 if (!done)
2606 return 0;
2607
2608 set_server_check_status(&s->check, HCHK_STATUS_L7RSP,
2609 "HTTP content check could not find a response body");
2610 return 1;
2611 }
2612
2613 /* Check that response body is not empty... */
2614 if (*contentptr == '\0') {
2615 if (!done)
2616 return 0;
2617
2618 set_server_check_status(&s->check, HCHK_STATUS_L7RSP,
2619 "HTTP content check found empty response body");
2620 return 1;
2621 }
2622
2623 /* Check the response content against the supplied string
2624 * or regex... */
2625 if ((s->proxy->options2 & PR_O2_EXP_TYPE0x03800000) == PR_O2_EXP_STR0x01800000)
2626 ret = strstr(contentptr, s->proxy->expect_str) != NULL((void*)0);
2627 else
2628 ret = regex_exec(s->proxy->expect_regex, contentptr);
2629
2630 /* if we don't match, we may need to wait more */
2631 if (!ret && !done)
2632 return 0;
2633
2634 if (ret) {
2635 /* content matched */
2636 if (s->proxy->options2 & PR_O2_EXP_INV0x04000000)
2637 set_server_check_status(&s->check, HCHK_STATUS_L7RSP,
2638 "HTTP check matched unwanted content");
2639 else
2640 set_server_check_status(&s->check, HCHK_STATUS_L7OKD,
2641 "HTTP content check matched");
2642 }
2643 else {
2644 if (s->proxy->options2 & PR_O2_EXP_INV0x04000000)
2645 set_server_check_status(&s->check, HCHK_STATUS_L7OKD,
2646 "HTTP check did not match unwanted content");
2647 else
2648 set_server_check_status(&s->check, HCHK_STATUS_L7RSP,
2649 "HTTP content check did not match");
2650 }
2651 break;
2652 }
2653 return 1;
2654}
2655
2656/*
2657 * return the id of a step in a send/expect session
2658 */
2659static int tcpcheck_get_step_id(struct check *check)
2660{
2661 struct tcpcheck_rule *cur = NULL((void*)0), *next = NULL((void*)0);
2662 int i = 0;
2663
2664 /* not even started anything yet => step 0 = initial connect */
2665 if (!check->current_step)
2666 return 0;
2667
2668 cur = check->last_started_step;
2669
2670 /* no step => first step */
2671 if (cur == NULL((void*)0))
2672 return 1;
2673
2674 /* increment i until current step */
2675 list_for_each_entry(next, check->tcpcheck_rules, list)for (next = ((typeof(next))(((const char *)((check->tcpcheck_rules
)->n)) - ((size_t)&((typeof(next))((void*)0))->list
))); &next->list != (check->tcpcheck_rules); next =
((typeof(next))(((const char *)(next->list.n)) - ((size_t
)&((typeof(next))((void*)0))->list)))) {
2676 if (next->list.p == &cur->list)
2677 break;
2678 ++i;
2679 }
2680
2681 return i;
2682}
2683
2684/*
2685 * return the latest known comment before (including) the given stepid
2686 * returns NULL if no comment found
2687 */
2688static char * tcpcheck_get_step_comment(struct check *check, int stepid)
2689{
2690 struct tcpcheck_rule *cur = NULL((void*)0);
2691 char *ret = NULL((void*)0);
2692 int i = 0;
2693
2694 /* not even started anything yet, return latest comment found before any action */
2695 if (!check->current_step) {
2696 list_for_each_entry(cur, check->tcpcheck_rules, list)for (cur = ((typeof(cur))(((const char *)((check->tcpcheck_rules
)->n)) - ((size_t)&((typeof(cur))((void*)0))->list)
)); &cur->list != (check->tcpcheck_rules); cur = ((
typeof(cur))(((const char *)(cur->list.n)) - ((size_t)&
((typeof(cur))((void*)0))->list)))) {
2697 if (cur->action == TCPCHK_ACT_COMMENT)
2698 ret = cur->comment;
2699 else
2700 goto return_comment;
2701 }
2702 }
2703
2704 i = 1;
2705 list_for_each_entry(cur, check->tcpcheck_rules, list)for (cur = ((typeof(cur))(((const char *)((check->tcpcheck_rules
)->n)) - ((size_t)&((typeof(cur))((void*)0))->list)
)); &cur->list != (check->tcpcheck_rules); cur = ((
typeof(cur))(((const char *)(cur->list.n)) - ((size_t)&
((typeof(cur))((void*)0))->list)))) {
2706 if (cur->comment)
2707 ret = cur->comment;
2708
2709 if (i >= stepid)
2710 goto return_comment;
2711
2712 ++i;
2713 }

2744 /* We have 4 possibilities here :
2745 * 1. we've not yet attempted step 1, and step 1 is a connect, so no
2746 * connection attempt was made yet ; conn==NULL;current_step==NULL.
2747 * 2. we've not yet attempted step 1, and step 1 is a not connect or
2748 * does not exist (no rule), so a connection attempt was made
2749 * before coming here, conn!=NULL.
2750 * 3. we're coming back after having started with step 1, so we may
2751 * be waiting for a connection attempt to complete. conn!=NULL.
2752 * 4. the connection + handshake are complete. conn!=NULL.
2753 *
2754 * #2 and #3 are quite similar, we want both the connection and the

3243
3244 /* cleanup before leaving */
3245 check->current_step = NULL((void*)0);
3246
3247 if (check->result == CHK_RES_FAILED)

←
Assuming field 'result' is equal to CHK_RES_FAILED
→
14
←
Taking true branch
→

15
←
Access to field 'flags' results in a dereference of a null pointer (loaded from variable 'conn')
3249
3250 out:
3251 return retcode;
3252}
3253
3254const char *init_check(struct check *check, int type)
3255{
3256 check->type = type;
3257
3258 b_reset(&check->bi); check->bi.size = global.tune.chksize;
3259 b_reset(&check->bo); check->bo.size = global.tune.chksize;
3260
3261 check->bi.area = calloc(check->bi.size, sizeof(char));
3262 check->bo.area = calloc(check->bo.size, sizeof(char));
3263
3264 if (!check->bi.area || !check->bo.area)
3265 return "out of memory while allocating check buffer";
3266
3267 check->wait_list.tasklet = tasklet_new();
3268 if (!check->wait_list.tasklet)
3269 return "out of memory while allocating check tasklet";
3270 check->wait_list.events = 0;
3271 check->wait_list.tasklet->process = event_srv_chk_io;
3272 check->wait_list.tasklet->context = check;
3273 return NULL((void*)0);
3274}
3275
3276void free_check(struct check *check)
3277{
3278 free(check->bi.area);
3279 free(check->bo.area);
3280 if (check->cs) {
3281 free(check->cs->conn);
3282 check->cs->conn = NULL((void*)0);
3283 cs_free(check->cs);
3284 check->cs = NULL((void*)0);
3285 }
3286}

3346/* Initializes mailer alerts for the proxy <p> using <mls> parameters.
3347 *
3348 * The function returns 1 in success case, otherwise, it returns 0 and err is
3349 * filled.
3350 */
3351int init_email_alert(struct mailers *mls, struct proxy *p, char **err)
3352{
3353 struct mailer *mailer;
3354 struct email_alertq *queues;
3355 const char *err_str;
3356 int i = 0;
3357
3358 if ((queues = calloc(mls->count, sizeof(*queues))) == NULL((void*)0)) {
3359 memprintf(err, "out of memory while allocating mailer alerts queues");
3360 goto fail_no_queue;
3361 }
3362
3363 for (mailer = mls->mailer_list; mailer; i++, mailer = mailer->next) {
3364 struct email_alertq *q = &queues[i];
3365 struct check *check = &q->check;
3366 struct task *t;
3367
3368 LIST_INIT(&q->email_alerts)((&q->email_alerts)->n = (&q->email_alerts)->
p = (&q->email_alerts));
3369 HA_SPIN_INIT(&q->lock)({ (*&q->lock) = 0; });
3370 check->inter = mls->timeout.mail;
3371 check->rise = DEF_AGENT_RISETIME1;
3372 check->proxy = p;
3373 check->fall = DEF_AGENT_FALLTIME1;
3374 if ((err_str = init_check(check, PR_O2_TCPCHK_CHK0x90000000))) {
3375 memprintf(err, "%s", err_str);
3376 goto error;
3377 }
3378
3379 check->xprt = mailer->xprt;
3380 check->addr = mailer->addr;
3381 check->port = get_host_port(&mailer->addr);
3382
3383 if ((t = task_new(MAX_THREADS_MASK(~0UL >> (((unsigned int)sizeof(long) * 8) - ((unsigned
int)sizeof(long) * 8))))) == NULL((void*)0)) {
3384 memprintf(err, "out of memory while allocating mailer alerts task");
3385 goto error;
3386 }
3387
3388 check->task = t;
3389 t->process = process_email_alert;
3390 t->context = check;
3391
3392 /* check this in one ms */
3393 t->expire = TICK_ETERNITY0;
3394 check->start = now;
3395 task_queue(t);
3396 }
3397
3398 mls->users++;
3399 free(p->email_alert.mailers.name);
3400 p->email_alert.mailers.m = mls;
3401 p->email_alert.queues = queues;
3402 return 0;
3403
3404 error:
3405 for (i = 0; i < mls->count; i++) {
3406 struct email_alertq *q = &queues[i];
3407 struct check *check = &q->check;
3408
3409 task_destroy(check->task);
3410 free_check(check);
3411 }
3412 free(queues);
3413 fail_no_queue:
3414 return 1;
3415}

3418static int add_tcpcheck_expect_str(struct list *list, const char *str)
3419{
3420 struct tcpcheck_rule *tcpcheck;
3421
3422 if ((tcpcheck = pool_alloc(pool_head_tcpcheck_rule)) == NULL((void*)0))
3423 return 0;

3425 tcpcheck->action = TCPCHK_ACT_EXPECT;
3426 tcpcheck->string = strdup(str);
3427 tcpcheck->expect_regex = NULL((void*)0);
3428 tcpcheck->comment = NULL((void*)0);
3429 if (!tcpcheck->string) {
3430 pool_free(pool_head_tcpcheck_rule, tcpcheck);
3431 return 0;
3432 }
3433
3434 LIST_ADDQ(list, &tcpcheck->list)({ (&tcpcheck->list)->p = (list)->p; (&tcpcheck
->list)->p->n = (list)->p = (&tcpcheck->list
); (&tcpcheck->list)->n = (list); (&tcpcheck->
list); });
3435 return 1;

3438static int add_tcpcheck_send_strs(struct list *list, const char * const *strs)
3439{
3440 struct tcpcheck_rule *tcpcheck;
3441 const char *in;
3442 char *dst;
3443 int i;
3444
3445 if ((tcpcheck = pool_alloc(pool_head_tcpcheck_rule)) == NULL((void*)0))
3446 return 0;
3447 memset(tcpcheck, 0, sizeof(*tcpcheck));
3448 tcpcheck->action = TCPCHK_ACT_SEND;
3449 tcpcheck->expect_regex = NULL((void*)0);
3450 tcpcheck->comment = NULL((void*)0);
3451 tcpcheck->string_len = 0;
3452 for (i = 0; strs[i]; i++)
3453 tcpcheck->string_len += strlen(strs[i]);
3454
3455 tcpcheck->string = malloc(tcpcheck->string_len + 1);
3456 if (!tcpcheck->string) {
3457 pool_free(pool_head_tcpcheck_rule, tcpcheck);
3458 return 0;
3459 }
3460
3461 dst = tcpcheck->string;
3462 for (i = 0; strs[i]; i++)
3463 for (in = strs[i]; (*dst = *in++); dst++);
3464 *dst = 0;
3465
3466 LIST_ADDQ(list, &tcpcheck->list)({ (&tcpcheck->list)->p = (list)->p; (&tcpcheck
->list)->p->n = (list)->p = (&tcpcheck->list
); (&tcpcheck->list)->n = (list); (&tcpcheck->
list); });
3467 return 1;
3468}

3578
3579static void enqueue_email_alert(struct proxy *p, struct server *s, const char *msg)
3580{
3581 int i;
3582 struct mailer *mailer;
3583
3584 for (i = 0, mailer = p->email_alert.mailers.m->mailer_list;
3585 i < p->email_alert.mailers.m->count; i++, mailer = mailer->next) {
3586 if (!enqueue_one_email_alert(p, s, &p->email_alert.queues[i], msg)) {
3587 ha_alert("Email alert [%s] could not be enqueued: out of memory\n", p->id);
3588 return;
3589 }
3590 }
3591
3592 return;
3593}
3594
3595/*
3596 * Send email alert if configured.
3597 */
3598void send_email_alert(struct server *s, int level, const char *format, ...)
3599{
3600 va_list argp;
3601 char buf[1024];
3602 int len;
3603 struct proxy *p = s->proxy;
3604
3605 if (!p->email_alert.mailers.m || level > p->email_alert.level || format == NULL((void*)0))
3606 return;
3607
3608 va_start(argp, format)__builtin_va_start(argp, format);
3609 len = vsnprintf(buf, sizeof(buf), format, argp);
3610 va_end(argp)__builtin_va_end(argp);
3611
3612 if (len < 0 || len >= sizeof(buf)) {
3613 ha_alert("Email alert [%s] could not format message\n", p->id);
3614 return;
3615 }
3616
3617 enqueue_email_alert(p, s, buf);
3618}
3619
3620/*
3621 * Return value:
3622 * the port to be used for the health check
3623 * 0 in case no port could be found for the check
3624 */
3625int srv_check_healthcheck_port(struct check *chk)
3626{
3627 int i = 0;
3628 struct server *srv = NULL((void*)0);
3629
3630 srv = chk->server;
3631
3632 /* If neither a port nor an addr was specified and no check transport
3633 * layer is forced, then the transport layer used by the checks is the
3634 * same as for the production traffic. Otherwise we use raw_sock by
3635 * default, unless one is specified.
3636 */
3637 if (!chk->port && !is_addr(&chk->addr)) {
3638 chk->use_ssl |= (srv->use_ssl || (srv->proxy->options & PR_O_TCPCHK_SSL0x08000000));
3639 chk->send_proxy |= (srv->pp_opts);
3640 }
3641
3642 /* by default, we use the health check port ocnfigured */
3643 if (chk->port > 0)
3644 return chk->port;
3645
3646 /* try to get the port from check_core.addr if check.port not set */
3647 i = get_host_port(&chk->addr);
3648 if (i > 0)
3649 return i;
3650
3651 /* try to get the port from server address */
3652 /* prevent MAPPORTS from working at this point, since checks could
3653 * not be performed in such case (MAPPORTS impose a relative ports
3654 * based on live traffic)
3655 */
3656 if (srv->flags & SRV_F_MAPPORTS0x0002)
3657 return 0;
3658
3659 i = srv->svc_port; /* by default */
3660 if (i > 0)
3661 return i;
3662
3663 return 0;
3664}

"__stop_init_STG_REGISTER"); static const struct initcall *__initcb_3666
__attribute__((__used__,__section__("init_" "STG_REGISTER"))

= (void *)(0), } : ((void*)0);

74
75/* returns true is the transport layer is ready */
76static inline int conn_xprt_ready(const struct connection *conn)
77{
78 return (conn->flags & CO_FL_XPRT_READY);
79}
80
81/* returns true is the control layer is ready */
82static inline int conn_ctrl_ready(const struct connection *conn)
83{
84 return (conn->flags & CO_FL_CTRL_READY);
85}
86
87/* Calls the init() function of the transport layer if any and if not done yet,
88 * and sets the CO_FL_XPRT_READY flag to indicate it was properly initialized.
89 * Returns <0 in case of error.
90 */
91static inline int conn_xprt_init(struct connection *conn)
92{
93 int ret = 0;
94
95 if (!conn_xprt_ready(conn) && conn->xprt && conn->xprt->init)
96 ret = conn->xprt->init(conn, &conn->xprt_ctx);
97
98 if (ret >= 0)
99 conn->flags |= CO_FL_XPRT_READY;
100
101 return ret;
102}
103
104/* Calls the close() function of the transport layer if any and if not done
105 * yet, and clears the CO_FL_XPRT_READY flag. However this is not done if the
106 * CO_FL_XPRT_TRACKED flag is set, which allows logs to take data from the
107 * transport layer very late if needed.
108 */
109static inline void conn_xprt_close(struct connection *conn)
110{
111 if ((conn->flags & (CO_FL_XPRT_READY|CO_FL_XPRT_TRACKED)) == CO_FL_XPRT_READY) {
112 if (conn->xprt->close)
113 conn->xprt->close(conn, conn->xprt_ctx);
114 conn->xprt_ctx = NULL((void*)0);
115 conn->flags &= ~CO_FL_XPRT_READY;
116 }
117}
118
119/* Initializes the connection's control layer which essentially consists in
120 * registering the file descriptor for polling and setting the CO_FL_CTRL_READY
121 * flag. The caller is responsible for ensuring that the control layer is
122 * already assigned to the connection prior to the call.
123 */
124static inline void conn_ctrl_init(struct connection *conn)
125{
126 if (!conn_ctrl_ready(conn)) {
127 int fd = conn->handle.fd;
128
129 fd_insert(fd, conn, conn_fd_handler, tid_bit);
130 conn->flags |= CO_FL_CTRL_READY;
131 }
132}
133
134/* Deletes the FD if the transport layer is already gone. Once done,
135 * it then removes the CO_FL_CTRL_READY flag.
136 */
137static inline void conn_ctrl_close(struct connection *conn)
138{
139 if ((conn->flags & (CO_FL_XPRT_READY|CO_FL_CTRL_READY)) == CO_FL_CTRL_READY) {
140 fd_delete(conn->handle.fd);
141 conn->handle.fd = DEAD_FD_MAGIC0xFDDEADFD;
142 conn->flags &= ~CO_FL_CTRL_READY;
143 }
144}
145
146/* If the connection still has a transport layer, then call its close() function
147 * if any, and delete the file descriptor if a control layer is set. This is
148 * used to close everything at once and atomically. However this is not done if
149 * the CO_FL_XPRT_TRACKED flag is set, which allows logs to take data from the
150 * transport layer very late if needed.
151 */
152static inline void conn_full_close(struct connection *conn)
153{
154 conn_xprt_close(conn);
155 conn_ctrl_close(conn);
156}
157
158/* stop tracking a connection, allowing conn_full_close() to always
159 * succeed.
160 */
161static inline void conn_stop_tracking(struct connection *conn)
162{
163 conn->flags &= ~CO_FL_XPRT_TRACKED;
164}
165
166/* Stop all polling on the fd. This might be used when an error is encountered
167 * for example.
168 */
169static inline void conn_stop_polling(struct connection *c)
170{
171 if (conn_ctrl_ready(c))
172 fd_stop_both(c->handle.fd);
173}
174
175/* Stops polling in case of error on the connection. */
176static inline void conn_cond_update_polling(struct connection *c)
177{
178 if (unlikely(c->flags & CO_FL_ERROR)(__builtin_expect((c->flags & CO_FL_ERROR) != 0, 0)))
179 conn_stop_polling(c);
180}
181
182/* read shutdown, called from the rcv_buf/rcv_pipe handlers when
183 * detecting an end of connection.
184 */
185static inline void conn_sock_read0(struct connection *c)
186{
187 c->flags |= CO_FL_SOCK_RD_SH;
188 if (conn_ctrl_ready(c)) {
189 fd_stop_recv(c->handle.fd);
190 /* we don't risk keeping ports unusable if we found the
191 * zero from the other side.
192 */
193 fdtab[c->handle.fd].linger_risk = 0;
194 }
195}
196
197/* write shutdown, indication that the upper layer is not willing to send
198 * anything anymore and wants to close after pending data are sent. The
199 * <clean> argument will allow not to perform the socket layer shutdown if
200 * equal to 0.
201 */
202static inline void conn_sock_shutw(struct connection *c, int clean)
203{
204 c->flags |= CO_FL_SOCK_WR_SH;
205 if (conn_ctrl_ready(c)) {
206 fd_stop_send(c->handle.fd);
207 /* don't perform a clean shutdown if we're going to reset or
208 * if the shutr was already received.
209 */
210 if (!(c->flags & CO_FL_SOCK_RD_SH) && clean)
211 shutdown(c->handle.fd, SHUT_WRSHUT_WR);
212 }
213}
214
215static inline void conn_xprt_shutw(struct connection *c)
216{
217 if (conn_ctrl_ready(c))
218 fd_stop_send(c->handle.fd);
219
220 /* clean data-layer shutdown */
221 if (c->xprt && c->xprt->shutw)
222 c->xprt->shutw(c, c->xprt_ctx, 1);
223}
224
225static inline void conn_xprt_shutw_hard(struct connection *c)
226{
227 if (conn_ctrl_ready(c))
228 fd_stop_send(c->handle.fd);
229
230 /* unclean data-layer shutdown */
231 if (c->xprt && c->xprt->shutw)
232 c->xprt->shutw(c, c->xprt_ctx, 0);
233}
234
235/* shut read */
236static inline void cs_shutr(struct conn_stream *cs, enum cs_shr_mode mode)
237{
238
239 /* clean data-layer shutdown */
240 if (cs->conn->mux && cs->conn->mux->shutr)
241 cs->conn->mux->shutr(cs, mode);
242 cs->flags |= (mode == CS_SHR_DRAIN) ? CS_FL_SHRD : CS_FL_SHRR;
243}
244
245/* shut write */
246static inline void cs_shutw(struct conn_stream *cs, enum cs_shw_mode mode)
247{
248
249 /* clean data-layer shutdown */
250 if (cs->conn->mux && cs->conn->mux->shutw)
251 cs->conn->mux->shutw(cs, mode);
252 cs->flags |= (mode == CS_SHW_NORMAL) ? CS_FL_SHWN : CS_FL_SHWS;
253}
254
255/* completely close a conn_stream (but do not detach it) */
256static inline void cs_close(struct conn_stream *cs)
257{
258 cs_shutw(cs, CS_SHW_SILENT);
259 cs_shutr(cs, CS_SHR_RESET);
260 cs->flags = CS_FL_NONE;
261}
262
263/* sets CS_FL_ERROR or CS_FL_ERR_PENDING on the cs */
264static inline void cs_set_error(struct conn_stream *cs)
265{
266 if (cs->flags & CS_FL_EOS)
267 cs->flags |= CS_FL_ERROR;
268 else
269 cs->flags |= CS_FL_ERR_PENDING;
270}
271
272/* detect sock->data read0 transition */
273static inline int conn_xprt_read0_pending(struct connection *c)
274{
275 return (c->flags & CO_FL_SOCK_RD_SH) != 0;
276}
277
278/* prepares a connection to work with protocol <proto> and transport <xprt>.
279 * The transport's is initialized as well, and the mux and its context are
280 * cleared. The target is not reinitialized and it is recommended that it is
281 * set prior to calling this function so that the function may make use of it
282 * in the future to refine the mux choice if needed.
283 */
284static inline void conn_prepare(struct connection *conn, const struct protocol *proto, const struct xprt_ops *xprt)
285{
286 conn->ctrl = proto;
287 conn->xprt = xprt;
288 conn->mux = NULL((void*)0);
289 conn->xprt_ctx = NULL((void*)0);
290 conn->ctx = NULL((void*)0);
291}
292
293/*
294 * Initializes all required fields for a new conn_strema.
295 */
296static inline void cs_init(struct conn_stream *cs, struct connection *conn)
297{
298 cs->obj_type = OBJ_TYPE_CS;
299 cs->flags = CS_FL_NONE;
300 cs->conn = conn;
301}
302
303/* Initializes all required fields for a new connection. Note that it does the
304 * minimum acceptable initialization for a connection that already exists and
305 * is about to be reused. It also leaves the addresses untouched, which makes
306 * it usable across connection retries to reset a connection to a known state.
307 */
308static inline void conn_init(struct connection *conn)
309{
310 conn->obj_type = OBJ_TYPE_CONN;
311 conn->flags = CO_FL_NONE;
312 conn->mux = NULL((void*)0);
313 conn->ctx = NULL((void*)0);
314 conn->owner = NULL((void*)0);
315 conn->send_proxy_ofs = 0;
316 conn->handle.fd = DEAD_FD_MAGIC0xFDDEADFD;
317 conn->err_code = CO_ER_NONE;
318 conn->target = NULL((void*)0);
319 conn->destroy_cb = NULL((void*)0);
320 conn->proxy_netns = NULL((void*)0);
321 MT_LIST_INIT(&conn->list)((&conn->list)->next = (&conn->list)->prev
= (&conn->list));
322 LIST_INIT(&conn->session_list)((&conn->session_list)->n = (&conn->session_list
)->p = (&conn->session_list));
323 conn->subs = NULL((void*)0);
324 conn->idle_time = 0;
325 conn->src = NULL((void*)0);
326 conn->dst = NULL((void*)0);
327 conn->proxy_authority = NULL((void*)0);
328 conn->proxy_unique_id = IST_NULL((const struct ist){ .ptr = 0, .len = 0 });
329}
330
331/* sets <owner> as the connection's owner */
332static inline void conn_set_owner(struct connection *conn, void *owner, void (*cb)(struct connection *))
333{
334 conn->owner = owner;
335 conn->destroy_cb = cb;
336}
337
338/* Allocates a struct sockaddr from the pool if needed, assigns it to *sap and
339 * returns it. If <sap> is NULL, the address is always allocated and returned.
340 * if <sap> is non-null, an address will only be allocated if it points to a
341 * non-null pointer. In this case the allocated address will be assigned there.
342 * In both situations the new pointer is returned.
343 */
344static inline struct sockaddr_storage *sockaddr_alloc(struct sockaddr_storage **sap)
345{
346 struct sockaddr_storage *sa;
347
348 if (sap && *sap)
349 return *sap;
350
351 sa = pool_alloc(pool_head_sockaddr);
352 if (sap)
353 *sap = sa;
354 return sa;
355}
356
357/* Releases the struct sockaddr potentially pointed to by <sap> to the pool. It
358 * may be NULL or may point to NULL. If <sap> is not NULL, a NULL is placed
359 * there.
360 */
361static inline void sockaddr_free(struct sockaddr_storage **sap)
362{
363 if (!sap)
364 return;
365 pool_free(pool_head_sockaddr, *sap);
366 *sap = NULL((void*)0);
367}
368
369/* Tries to allocate a new connection and initialized its main fields. The
370 * connection is returned on success, NULL on failure. The connection must
371 * be released using pool_free() or conn_free().
372 */
373static inline struct connection *conn_new()
374{
375 struct connection *conn;
376
377 conn = pool_alloc(pool_head_connection);
378 if (likely(conn != NULL)(__builtin_expect((conn != ((void*)0)) != 0, 1)))
379 conn_init(conn);
380 return conn;
381}
382
383/* Releases a conn_stream previously allocated by cs_new(), as well as any
384 * buffer it would still hold.
385 */
386static inline void cs_free(struct conn_stream *cs)
387{
388
389 pool_free(pool_head_connstream, cs);
390}
391
392/* Tries to allocate a new conn_stream and initialize its main fields. If
393 * <conn> is NULL, then a new connection is allocated on the fly, initialized,
394 * and assigned to cs->conn ; this connection will then have to be released
395 * using pool_free() or conn_free(). The conn_stream is initialized and added
396 * to the mux's stream list on success, then returned. On failure, nothing is
397 * allocated and NULL is returned.
398 */
399static inline struct conn_stream *cs_new(struct connection *conn)
400{
401 struct conn_stream *cs;
402
403 cs = pool_alloc(pool_head_connstream);
404 if (unlikely(!cs)(__builtin_expect((!cs) != 0, 0)))
405 return NULL((void*)0);
406
407 if (!conn) {
408 conn = conn_new();
409 if (unlikely(!conn)(__builtin_expect((!conn) != 0, 0))) {
410 cs_free(cs);
411 return NULL((void*)0);
412 }
413 conn_init(conn);
414 }
415
416 cs_init(cs, conn);
417 return cs;
418}
419
420/* Retrieves any valid conn_stream from this connection, preferably the first
421 * valid one. The purpose is to be able to figure one other end of a private
422 * connection for purposes like source binding or proxy protocol header
423 * emission. In such cases, any conn_stream is expected to be valid so the
424 * mux is encouraged to return the first one it finds. If the connection has
425 * no mux or the mux has no get_first_cs() method or the mux has no valid
426 * conn_stream, NULL is returned. The output pointer is purposely marked
427 * const to discourage the caller from modifying anything there.
428 */
429static inline const struct conn_stream *cs_get_first(const struct connection *conn)
430{
431 if (!conn || !conn->mux || !conn->mux->get_first_cs)
432 return NULL((void*)0);
433 return conn->mux->get_first_cs(conn);
434}
435
436static inline void conn_force_unsubscribe(struct connection *conn)
437{
438 if (!conn->subs)
439 return;
440 conn->subs->events = 0;
441 conn->subs = NULL((void*)0);
442}
443
444/* Releases a connection previously allocated by conn_new() */
445static inline void conn_free(struct connection *conn)
446{

451 sess->idle_conns--;

455 sockaddr_free(&conn->src);
456 sockaddr_free(&conn->dst);
457
458 if (conn->proxy_authority != NULL((void*)0)) {
459 pool_free(pool_head_authority, conn->proxy_authority);

461 }

465 }

496/* Release a conn_stream */
497static inline void cs_destroy(struct conn_stream *cs)
498{
499 if (cs->conn->mux)
500 cs->conn->mux->detach(cs);
501 else {
502 /* It's too early to have a mux, let's just destroy
503 * the connection
504 */
505 struct connection *conn = cs->conn;
506
507 conn_stop_tracking(conn);
508 conn_full_close(conn);
509 if (conn->destroy_cb)
510 conn->destroy_cb(conn);
511 conn_free(conn);
512 }
513 cs_free(cs);
514}

517static inline struct connection *cs_conn(const struct conn_stream *cs)
518{
519 return cs ? cs->conn : NULL((void*)0);

520}

522/* Retrieves the connection's original source address. Returns non-zero on
523 * success or zero on failure. The operation is only performed once and the
524 * address is stored in the connection for future use.
525 */
526static inline int conn_get_src(struct connection *conn)
527{
528 if (conn->flags & CO_FL_ADDR_FROM_SET)
529 return 1;
530
531 if (!conn_ctrl_ready(conn) || !conn->ctrl->get_src)
532 return 0;
533
534 if (!sockaddr_alloc(&conn->src))
535 return 0;
536
537 if (conn->ctrl->get_src(conn->handle.fd, (struct sockaddr *)conn->src,
538 sizeof(*conn->src),
539 obj_type(conn->target) != OBJ_TYPE_LISTENER) == -1)
540 return 0;
541 conn->flags |= CO_FL_ADDR_FROM_SET;
542 return 1;
543}
544
545/* Retrieves the connection's original destination address. Returns non-zero on
546 * success or zero on failure. The operation is only performed once and the
547 * address is stored in the connection for future use.
548 */
549static inline int conn_get_dst(struct connection *conn)
550{
551 if (conn->flags & CO_FL_ADDR_TO_SET)
552 return 1;
553
554 if (!conn_ctrl_ready(conn) || !conn->ctrl->get_dst)
555 return 0;
556
557 if (!sockaddr_alloc(&conn->dst))
558 return 0;
559
560 if (conn->ctrl->get_dst(conn->handle.fd, (struct sockaddr *)conn->dst,
561 sizeof(*conn->dst),
562 obj_type(conn->target) != OBJ_TYPE_LISTENER) == -1)
563 return 0;
564 conn->flags |= CO_FL_ADDR_TO_SET;
565 return 1;
566}
567
568/* Sets the TOS header in IPv4 and the traffic class header in IPv6 packets
569 * (as per RFC3260 #4 and BCP37 #4.2 and #5.2). The connection is tested and if
570 * it is null, nothing is done.
571 */
572static inline void conn_set_tos(const struct connection *conn, int tos)
573{
574 if (!conn || !conn_ctrl_ready(conn))
575 return;
576
577#ifdef IP_TOS1
578 if (conn->src->ss_family == AF_INET2)
579 setsockopt(conn->handle.fd, IPPROTO_IPIPPROTO_IP, IP_TOS1, &tos, sizeof(tos));
580#endif
581#ifdef IPV6_TCLASS67
582 if (conn->src->ss_family == AF_INET610) {
583 if (IN6_IS_ADDR_V4MAPPED(&((struct sockaddr_in6 *)conn->src)->sin6_addr)(__extension__ ({ const struct in6_addr *__a = (const struct in6_addr
*) (&((struct sockaddr_in6 *)conn->src)->sin6_addr
); __a->__in6_u.__u6_addr32[0] == 0 && __a->__in6_u
.__u6_addr32[1] == 0 && __a->__in6_u.__u6_addr32[2
] == __bswap_32 (0xffff); })))
584 /* v4-mapped addresses need IP_TOS */
585 setsockopt(conn->handle.fd, IPPROTO_IPIPPROTO_IP, IP_TOS1, &tos, sizeof(tos));
586 else
587 setsockopt(conn->handle.fd, IPPROTO_IPV6IPPROTO_IPV6, IPV6_TCLASS67, &tos, sizeof(tos));
588 }
589#endif
590}
591
592/* Sets the netfilter mark on the connection's socket. The connection is tested
593 * and if it is null, nothing is done.
594 */
595static inline void conn_set_mark(const struct connection *conn, int mark)
596{
597 if (!conn || !conn_ctrl_ready(conn))
598 return;
599
600#ifdef SO_MARK36
601 setsockopt(conn->handle.fd, SOL_SOCKET1, SO_MARK36, &mark, sizeof(mark));
602#endif
603}
604
605/* Sets adjust the TCP quick-ack feature on the connection's socket. The
606 * connection is tested and if it is null, nothing is done.
607 */
608static inline void conn_set_quickack(const struct connection *conn, int value)
609{
610 if (!conn || !conn_ctrl_ready(conn))
611 return;
612
613#ifdef TCP_QUICKACK12
614 setsockopt(conn->handle.fd, IPPROTO_TCPIPPROTO_TCP, TCP_QUICKACK12, &value, sizeof(value));
615#endif
616}
617
618/* Attaches a conn_stream to a data layer and sets the relevant callbacks */
619static inline void cs_attach(struct conn_stream *cs, void *data, const struct data_cb *data_cb)
620{
621 cs->data_cb = data_cb;
622 cs->data = data;
623}
624
625static inline struct wait_event *wl_set_waitcb(struct wait_event *wl, struct task *(*cb)(struct task *, void *, unsigned short), void *ctx)
626{
627 if (!wl->tasklet->process) {
628 wl->tasklet->process = cb;
629 wl->tasklet->context = ctx;
630 }
631 return wl;
632}
633
634/* Installs the connection's mux layer for upper context <ctx>.
635 * Returns < 0 on error.
636 */
637static inline int conn_install_mux(struct connection *conn, const struct mux_ops *mux,
638 void *ctx, struct proxy *prx, struct session *sess)
639{
640 int ret;
641
642 conn->mux = mux;
643 conn->ctx = ctx;
644 ret = mux->init ? mux->init(conn, prx, sess, &BUF_NULL((struct buffer){ })) : 0;
645 if (ret < 0) {
646 conn->mux = NULL((void*)0);
647 conn->ctx = NULL((void*)0);
648 }
649 return ret;
650}

652/* returns a human-readable error code for conn->err_code, or NULL if the code
653 * is unknown.
654 */
655static inline const char *conn_err_code_str(struct connection *c)
656{
657 switch (c->err_code) {
658 case CO_ER_NONE: return "Success";
659
660 case CO_ER_CONF_FDLIM: return "Reached configured maxconn value";
661 case CO_ER_PROC_FDLIM: return "Too many sockets on the process";
662 case CO_ER_SYS_FDLIM: return "Too many sockets on the system";
663 case CO_ER_SYS_MEMLIM: return "Out of system buffers";
664 case CO_ER_NOPROTO: return "Protocol or address family not supported";
665 case CO_ER_SOCK_ERR: return "General socket error";
666 case CO_ER_PORT_RANGE: return "Source port range exhausted";
667 case CO_ER_CANT_BIND: return "Can't bind to source address";
668 case CO_ER_FREE_PORTS: return "Out of local source ports on the system";
669 case CO_ER_ADDR_INUSE: return "Local source address already in use";
670
671 case CO_ER_PRX_EMPTY: return "Connection closed while waiting for PROXY protocol header";
672 case CO_ER_PRX_ABORT: return "Connection error while waiting for PROXY protocol header";
673 case CO_ER_PRX_TIMEOUT: return "Timeout while waiting for PROXY protocol header";
674 case CO_ER_PRX_TRUNCATED: return "Truncated PROXY protocol header received";
675 case CO_ER_PRX_NOT_HDR: return "Received something which does not look like a PROXY protocol header";
676 case CO_ER_PRX_BAD_HDR: return "Received an invalid PROXY protocol header";
677 case CO_ER_PRX_BAD_PROTO: return "Received an unhandled protocol in the PROXY protocol header";
678
679 case CO_ER_CIP_EMPTY: return "Connection closed while waiting for NetScaler Client IP header";
680 case CO_ER_CIP_ABORT: return "Connection error while waiting for NetScaler Client IP header";
681 case CO_ER_CIP_TRUNCATED: return "Truncated NetScaler Client IP header received";
682 case CO_ER_CIP_BAD_MAGIC: return "Received an invalid NetScaler Client IP magic number";
683 case CO_ER_CIP_BAD_PROTO: return "Received an unhandled protocol in the NetScaler Client IP header";
684
685 case CO_ER_SSL_EMPTY: return "Connection closed during SSL handshake";
686 case CO_ER_SSL_ABORT: return "Connection error during SSL handshake";
687 case CO_ER_SSL_TIMEOUT: return "Timeout during SSL handshake";
688 case CO_ER_SSL_TOO_MANY: return "Too many SSL connections";
689 case CO_ER_SSL_NO_MEM: return "Out of memory when initializing an SSL connection";
690 case CO_ER_SSL_RENEG: return "Rejected a client-initiated SSL renegotiation attempt";
691 case CO_ER_SSL_CA_FAIL: return "SSL client CA chain cannot be verified";
692 case CO_ER_SSL_CRT_FAIL: return "SSL client certificate not trusted";
693 case CO_ER_SSL_MISMATCH: return "Server presented an SSL certificate different from the configured one";
694 case CO_ER_SSL_MISMATCH_SNI: return "Server presented an SSL certificate different from the expected one";
695 case CO_ER_SSL_HANDSHAKE: return "SSL handshake failure";
696 case CO_ER_SSL_HANDSHAKE_HB: return "SSL handshake failure after heartbeat";
697 case CO_ER_SSL_KILLED_HB: return "Stopped a TLSv1 heartbeat attack (CVE-2014-0160)";
698 case CO_ER_SSL_NO_TARGET: return "Attempt to use SSL on an unknown target (internal error)";
699
700 case CO_ER_SOCKS4_SEND: return "SOCKS4 Proxy write error during handshake";
701 case CO_ER_SOCKS4_RECV: return "SOCKS4 Proxy read error during handshake";
702 case CO_ER_SOCKS4_DENY: return "SOCKS4 Proxy deny the request";
703 case CO_ER_SOCKS4_ABORT: return "SOCKS4 Proxy handshake aborted by server";
704 }
705 return NULL((void*)0);
706}

718 return "NONE";

724 if (!conn || !conn->mux)
725 return "NONE";

735
736/* registers pointer to transport layer <id> (XPRT_*) */
737static inline void xprt_register(int id, struct xprt_ops *xprt)
738{
739 if (id >= XPRT_ENTRIES)
740 return;
741 registered_xprt[id] = xprt;
742}
743
744/* returns pointer to transport layer <id> (XPRT_*) or NULL if not registered */
745static inline struct xprt_ops *xprt_get(int id)
746{
747 if (id >= XPRT_ENTRIES)
748 return NULL((void*)0);
749 return registered_xprt[id];
750}
751
752/* Try to add a handshake pseudo-XPRT. If the connection's first XPRT is
753 * raw_sock, then just use the new XPRT as the connection XPRT, otherwise
754 * call the xprt's add_xprt() method.
755 * Returns 0 on success, or non-zero on failure.
756 */
757static inline int xprt_add_hs(struct connection *conn)
758{
759 void *xprt_ctx = NULL((void*)0);
760 const struct xprt_ops *ops = xprt_get(XPRT_HANDSHAKE);
761 void *nextxprt_ctx = NULL((void*)0);
762 const struct xprt_ops *nextxprt_ops = NULL((void*)0);
763
764 if (conn->flags & CO_FL_ERROR)
765 return -1;
766 if (ops->init(conn, &xprt_ctx) < 0)
767 return -1;
768 if (conn->xprt == xprt_get(XPRT_RAW)) {
769 nextxprt_ctx = conn->xprt_ctx;
770 nextxprt_ops = conn->xprt;
771 conn->xprt_ctx = xprt_ctx;
772 conn->xprt = ops;
773 } else {
774 if (conn->xprt->add_xprt(conn, conn->xprt_ctx, xprt_ctx, ops,
775 &nextxprt_ctx, &nextxprt_ops) != 0) {
776 ops->close(conn, xprt_ctx);
777 return -1;
778 }
779 }
780 if (ops->add_xprt(conn, xprt_ctx, nextxprt_ctx, nextxprt_ops, NULL((void*)0), NULL((void*)0)) != 0) {
781 ops->close(conn, xprt_ctx);
782 return -1;
783 }
784 return 0;
785}
786
787static inline int conn_get_alpn(const struct connection *conn, const char **str, int *len)
788{
789 if (!conn_xprt_ready(conn) || !conn->xprt->get_alpn)
790 return 0;
791 return conn->xprt->get_alpn(conn, conn->xprt_ctx, str, len);
792}

794/* registers proto mux list <list>. Modifies the list element! */
795static inline void register_mux_proto(struct mux_proto_list *list)
796{
797 LIST_ADDQ(&mux_proto_list.list, &list->list)({ (&list->list)->p = (&mux_proto_list.list)->
p; (&list->list)->p->n = (&mux_proto_list.list
)->p = (&list->list); (&list->list)->n = (
&mux_proto_list.list); (&list->list); });
798}
799
800/* unregisters proto mux list <list> */
801static inline void unregister_mux_proto(struct mux_proto_list *list)
802{
803 LIST_DEL(&list->list)({ typeof(&list->list) __ret = (&list->list); (
&list->list)->n->p = (&list->list)->p;
(&list->list)->p->n = (&list->list)->
n; (__ret); });
804 LIST_INIT(&list->list)((&list->list)->n = (&list->list)->p = (&
list->list));
805}
806
807static inline struct mux_proto_list *get_mux_proto(const struct ist proto)
808{
809 struct mux_proto_list *item;
810
811 list_for_each_entry(item, &mux_proto_list.list, list)for (item = ((typeof(item))(((const char *)((&mux_proto_list
.list)->n)) - ((size_t)&((typeof(item))((void*)0))->
list))); &item->list != (&mux_proto_list.list); item
= ((typeof(item))(((const char *)(item->list.n)) - ((size_t
)&((typeof(item))((void*)0))->list)))) {
812 if (isteq(proto, item->token))
813 return item;
814 }
815 return NULL((void*)0);
816}
817
818/* Lists the known proto mux on <out> */
819static inline void list_mux_proto(FILE *out)
820{
821 struct mux_proto_list *item;
822 struct ist proto;
823 char *mode, *side;
824
825 fprintf(out, "Available multiplexer protocols :\n"
826 "(protocols marked as <default> cannot be specified using 'proto' keyword)\n");
827 list_for_each_entry(item, &mux_proto_list.list, list)for (item = ((typeof(item))(((const char *)((&mux_proto_list
.list)->n)) - ((size_t)&((typeof(item))((void*)0))->
list))); &item->list != (&mux_proto_list.list); item
= ((typeof(item))(((const char *)(item->list.n)) - ((size_t
)&((typeof(item))((void*)0))->list)))) {
828 proto = item->token;
829
830 if (item->mode == PROTO_MODE_ANY)
831 mode = "TCP|HTTP";
832 else if (item->mode == PROTO_MODE_TCP)
833 mode = "TCP";
834 else if (item->mode == PROTO_MODE_HTTP)
835 mode = "HTTP";
836 else
837 mode = "NONE";
838
839 if (item->side == PROTO_SIDE_BOTH)
840 side = "FE|BE";
841 else if (item->side == PROTO_SIDE_FE)
842 side = "FE";
843 else if (item->side == PROTO_SIDE_BE)
844 side = "BE";
845 else
846 side = "NONE";
847
848 fprintf(out, " %15s : mode=%-10s side=%-8s mux=%s\n",
849 (proto.len ? proto.ptr : "<default>"), mode, side, item->mux->name);
850 }
851}
852
853/* returns the first mux entry in the list matching the exact same <mux_proto>
854 * and compatible with the <proto_side> (FE or BE) and the <proto_mode> (TCP or
855 * HTTP). <mux_proto> can be empty. Will fall back to the first compatible mux
856 * with exactly the same <proto_mode> or with an empty name. May return
857 * null if the code improperly registered the default mux to use as a fallback.
858 */
859static inline const struct mux_proto_list *conn_get_best_mux_entry(
860 const struct ist mux_proto,
861 int proto_side, int proto_mode)
862{
863 struct mux_proto_list *item;
864 struct mux_proto_list *fallback = NULL((void*)0);
865
866 list_for_each_entry(item, &mux_proto_list.list, list)for (item = ((typeof(item))(((const char *)((&mux_proto_list
.list)->n)) - ((size_t)&((typeof(item))((void*)0))->
list))); &item->list != (&mux_proto_list.list); item
= ((typeof(item))(((const char *)(item->list.n)) - ((size_t
)&((typeof(item))((void*)0))->list)))) {
867 if (!(item->side & proto_side) || !(item->mode & proto_mode))
868 continue;
869 if (istlen(mux_proto) && isteq(mux_proto, item->token))
870 return item;
871 else if (!istlen(item->token)) {
872 if (!fallback || (item->mode == proto_mode && fallback->mode != proto_mode))
873 fallback = item;
874 }
875 }
876 return fallback;
877
878}
879
880/* returns the first mux in the list matching the exact same <mux_proto> and
881 * compatible with the <proto_side> (FE or BE) and the <proto_mode> (TCP or
882 * HTTP). <mux_proto> can be empty. Will fall back to the first compatible mux
883 * with exactly the same <proto_mode> or with an empty name. May return
884 * null if the code improperly registered the default mux to use as a fallback.
885 */
886static inline const struct mux_ops *conn_get_best_mux(struct connection *conn,
887 const struct ist mux_proto,
888 int proto_side, int proto_mode)
889{
890 const struct mux_proto_list *item;
891
892 item = conn_get_best_mux_entry(mux_proto, proto_side, proto_mode);
893
894 return item ? item->mux : NULL((void*)0);
895}
896
897/* returns 0 if the connection is valid and is a frontend connection, otherwise
898 * returns 1 indicating it's a backend connection. And uninitialized connection
899 * also returns 1 to better handle the usage in the middle of initialization.
900 */
901static inline int conn_is_back(const struct connection *conn)
902{
903 return !objt_listener(conn->target);
904}
905
906/* returns a pointer to the proxy associated with this connection. For a front
907 * connection it returns a pointer to the frontend ; for a back connection, it
908 * returns a pointer to the backend.
909 */
910static inline struct proxy *conn_get_proxy(const struct connection *conn)
911{
912 struct listener *l;
913 struct server *s;
914
915 /* check if it's a frontend connection */
916 l = objt_listener(conn->target);
917 if (l)
918 return l->bind_conf->frontend;
919
920 /* check if it's a backend connection */
921 s = objt_server(conn->target);
922 if (s)
923 return s->proxy;
924
925 return objt_proxy(conn->target);
926}
927
928/* installs the best mux for incoming connection <conn> using the upper context
929 * <ctx>. If the mux protocol is forced, we use it to find the best
930 * mux. Otherwise we use the ALPN name, if any. Returns < 0 on error.
931 */
932static inline int conn_install_mux_fe(struct connection *conn, void *ctx)
933{
934 struct bind_conf *bind_conf = __objt_listener(conn->target)->bind_conf;
935 const struct mux_ops *mux_ops;
936
937 if (bind_conf->mux_proto)
938 mux_ops = bind_conf->mux_proto->mux;
939 else {
940 struct ist mux_proto;
941 const char *alpn_str = NULL((void*)0);
942 int alpn_len = 0;
943 int mode;
944
945 if (bind_conf->frontend->mode == PR_MODE_HTTP)
946 mode = PROTO_MODE_HTTP;
947 else
948 mode = PROTO_MODE_TCP;
949
950 conn_get_alpn(conn, &alpn_str, &alpn_len);
951 mux_proto = ist2(alpn_str, alpn_len);
952 mux_ops = conn_get_best_mux(conn, mux_proto, PROTO_SIDE_FE, mode);
953 if (!mux_ops)
954 return -1;
955 }
956 return conn_install_mux(conn, mux_ops, ctx, bind_conf->frontend, conn->owner);
957}
958
959/* installs the best mux for outgoing connection <conn> using the upper context
960 * <ctx>. If the mux protocol is forced, we use it to find the best mux. Returns
961 * < 0 on error.
962 */
963static inline int conn_install_mux_be(struct connection *conn, void *ctx, struct session *sess)
964{
965 struct server *srv = objt_server(conn->target);
966 struct proxy *prx = objt_proxy(conn->target);
967 const struct mux_ops *mux_ops;
968
969 if (srv)
970 prx = srv->proxy;
971
972 if (!prx) // target must be either proxy or server
973 return -1;
974
975 if (srv && srv->mux_proto)
976 mux_ops = srv->mux_proto->mux;
977 else {
978 struct ist mux_proto;
979 const char *alpn_str = NULL((void*)0);
980 int alpn_len = 0;
981 int mode;
982
983 if (prx->mode == PR_MODE_HTTP)
984 mode = PROTO_MODE_HTTP;
985 else
986 mode = PROTO_MODE_TCP;
987
988 conn_get_alpn(conn, &alpn_str, &alpn_len);
989 mux_proto = ist2(alpn_str, alpn_len);
990
991 mux_ops = conn_get_best_mux(conn, mux_proto, PROTO_SIDE_BE, mode);
992 if (!mux_ops)
993 return -1;
994 }
995 return conn_install_mux(conn, mux_ops, ctx, prx, sess);
996}
997
998/* Change the mux for the connection.
999 * The caller should make sure he's not subscribed to the underlying XPRT.
1000 */
1001static inline int conn_upgrade_mux_fe(struct connection *conn, void *ctx, struct buffer *buf,
1002 struct ist mux_proto, int mode)
1003{
1004 struct bind_conf *bind_conf = __objt_listener(conn->target)->bind_conf;
1005 const struct mux_ops *old_mux, *new_mux;
1006 void *old_mux_ctx;
1007 const char *alpn_str = NULL((void*)0);
1008 int alpn_len = 0;
1009
1010 if (!mux_proto.len) {
1011 conn_get_alpn(conn, &alpn_str, &alpn_len);
1012 mux_proto = ist2(alpn_str, alpn_len);
1013 }
1014 new_mux = conn_get_best_mux(conn, mux_proto, PROTO_SIDE_FE, mode);
1015 old_mux = conn->mux;
1016
1017 /* No mux found */
1018 if (!new_mux)
1019 return -1;
1020
1021 /* Same mux, nothing to do */
1022 if (old_mux == new_mux)
1023 return 0;
1024
1025 old_mux_ctx = conn->ctx;
1026 conn->mux = new_mux;
1027 conn->ctx = ctx;
1028 if (new_mux->init(conn, bind_conf->frontend, conn->owner, buf) == -1) {
1029 /* The mux upgrade failed, so restore the old mux */
1030 conn->ctx = old_mux_ctx;
1031 conn->mux = old_mux;
1032 return -1;
1033 }
1034
1035 /* The mux was upgraded, destroy the old one */
1036 *buf = BUF_NULL((struct buffer){ });
1037 old_mux->destroy(old_mux_ctx);
1038 return 0;
1039}
